  23. As a first time user of electric shavers, I was not impressed. The overall build quality is very good. It feels really nice in the hand, has a really good premium finish all over. I read some reviews that people thought it didn't click on well, but I actually was really confident in clicking the different heads on, and off. The little panel notifying you of it charging, or needing charge is well placed, and bright. The whole thing just has a nice feel to it. The shaver is really bad. It's really, really bad. Had to literally hold the thing to my skin for a good minute before it actually cleaned the stubble off my face. It is completely unusable, and I found myself going back to razors within about a month of trying to get used to using this thing. I currently have not used the shaving head for about 4 months. The body hair trimmer is okay. I'm a pretty hairy guy, so when I am trimming my hair though, a ton of s*** will get caught up in the comb really fast. An easy fix to that would be to have both ends of the comb be more open, allowing hair to be combed through one side and fall out the other. This is however not the case, and after trimming for a very short amount of time, I will find myself pulling the comb off, dumping all the hair, and combing again. This makes trimming extremely tedious. But, it works. And the length at which it does trim is a decent length. The beard trimmer is my favorite part. I do have a beard, it extends about half an inch off my face. I also have extremely curly black hair, so not trimming my beard makes it look like a bundle of hay. So I trim my beard about once a week with this, and so far I haven't really had any complaints on that end. It could be better, like the plastic head to the trimmer is ridiculously cheap, and with enough force I can push it down without using the lever. However, all my complaints with the trimmer really stem from that cheap plastic head. At the end of the day I wish I had returned this, and just bought a good beard trimmer. If you're looking for a good starter to electric shaving, don't get this. If you're looking for an okay body, and beard trimmer, consider this as an option.

  37. This Norelco Click and Style is the first electric shaver I have ever owned. I tried using a friends “foil” style shaver several years ago and didn’t like the shave it gave my face.<br />I am a blade shaver. I shave my head completely as well as my face. For the last year or so I’ve been growing a stubble type beard but have continued shaving my head and neck with a blade.<br />In order to keep my beard at a shorter length I have been using a Remington beard trimmer but it has quickly lost it’s battery life and blade sharpness so I decided to try out a different brand electric beard trimmer.<br />I came across this Click and Style and noticed the reviews were positive on it so I decided to give it a try. I also liked the idea of the different attachments that it offers. I figured I could use the beard Styler “trimmer” to replace my Remington and use the shaver head for my neck. I don’t do a lot of “below the neck line” shaving but figured I might start if I had a good shaver to use. Things are getting a little thick and scary down there.<br />The instructions say to use it for at least 3 weeks in order to condition your skin and get it used to electric razor shaving. After 1 week of use I have been extremely happy with the results I’m getting from the Norelco, even without any shaving cream or lotion.<br />The dual round shaving head does a great job on my neck. The beard trimmer provides me with a far better shave then the Remington ever did. It trims my beard at a very even length. I saw that some people had issues with the beard comb that Norelco either didn’t provide or whatever. The beard comb that came with mine works great. No issues there at all.<br />The battery life on it has been more then adequate as well. It doesn’t seem to take that long to charge (except for the first charge) and it has always been able to last me through both my beard and neck shaving and then some.<br />The only thing I find that it doesn’t do well is shave my head. I don’t think the face shaving attachment can articulate enough to provide a good close shave on a head. Either that or I am so used to getting a super close shave with my Headblade that nothing compares. I’m not concerned about the head shaving though, it was just something I thought I would try.<br />Changing from one attachment to the other is simple and quick, so is cleaning them. It's a comfortable shaver to hold and use. It's quiet and feels solid.<br />Overall, I would highly recommend this shaver. Especially for those that want a multi-purpose shaving tool that does it all really well. And it’s nice to see the price of replacement blades for the Click and Style aren’t very expensive. I can’t comment on how long they last but I won’t mind replacing them for what they cost.

I typically lather my face using a [[ASIN:B000WB4WVK badger silvertip shaving brush]] at home or use [[ASIN:B002TSOJGC Jack Black beard lube]] on the go and then shave with a [[ASIN:B003987CL0 Gillette Fusion proglide razor]]. I'm also preparing to learn to shave with a [[ASIN:B002P9BP3K straight razor]], although don't feel it's practical for my daily shaving routine. Shaving at the gym before work is more about convenience and efficiency.<br /><br />The Philips Norelco YS524/41 click & style shave toolkit, made in used China, uses a click on/off attachment system with a facial shaver, beard styler, and bodygroom shaver/trimmer. The shower proof, 100-240 volt razor takes an hour to charge and lasts for about 40 minutes of use. The razor is light in the hand and its contours provide comfortable holding. Registering the Philips Norelco YS524/41 shaver provides a 6 month warranty extension, plus shows tips and an instructional video.<br /><br />The facial shaver attachment blades are designed to last for twelve months of wet or dry shaving. While the shaver bodies have changed over time, the round shaving heads themselves do not appear to have changed at all. Shave by using both straight and circular motions, pulling skin tight where needed. The shaver will not cut or knick the skin, and can either be used dry or by applying shaving cream to the face. When using shaving cream, it may be necessary to reapply cream to ensure a thorough and consistent shave. Philips Norelco recommends using the shaver three times a week for several weeks so the face can adapt to this type of shaving and provide the best results.<br /><br />The beard styler with five length settings from 3/64 - 11/64 inches or 1 - 4.5mm is perfect for creating well kept stubble. I trim my beard with a #3 comb on a set of Walh clippers, which cuts to a 3/8&#34; or 9mm length. The comb settings lock into place and are stable during use and simply requires rinsing under water to clean. The maximum beard styler setting gets no where close to the length i need for trimming. Although, for those with a stubble length beards, this shaver kit may provide all in one convenience.<br /><br />The bodygroom shaver/trimmer uses rounded combs and tips to prevent skin irritation, and supposedly provide reliably smooth grooming anywhere below the neckline. Start with the comb to trim dry and clean hair to a length of 1/8 in/3mm before grooming in the shower. Unlike my beard, my body hair is soft and fine. Trimming body hair with this attachment was simple enough, and appeared smooth. However touch revealed sharp stubble, not exactly appealing for the person you may want to snuggle up with.<br /><br />For me, shaving with a razor at the gym is just as convenient, more efficient, and provides smoother results than using an electric razor. If you have course facial hair and are looking for a great shave, the Philips Norelco YS524 will probably disappoint. However if you're simply looking for a convenient no fuss shave on the go, the Philips Norelco YS524 may be for you.<br /><br />PROS:<br />45 day money back guarantee<br />Full 2-2.5 year warranty coverage<br />Cordless and shower proof<br /><br />CONS:<br />Could provide better resultsrd with a #3 comb on a set of Walh clippers, which cuts to a 3/8&#34; or 9mm length.   103. This Norelco face and body shaver and beard trimmer is a good deal if you plan to use all three functions. The face shaver is a two-headed version of Norelco's SensoTouch 2D flexing shaving head, and it works well on my face. When I first turned it on, it sounded underpowered, like the difference between an electric lawn trimmer and a gas-powered one. But I'd been using a decent foil shaver, which always left some neck hairs uncut no matter what I did, and the Norelco gets them all, and gives me a closer shave very comfortably, so forget how it sounds, it works. It feels light and is ergonomically shaped, and I now use the Norelco as my everyday face shaver. I don't find the fact that it has only two heads to be a problem at all. You can substitute a three-rotor SensoTouch head if you want, but unless you already have one I don't think buying one is worthwhile. The shaver is wet/dry, and can be used in the shower and with shaving cream, but frankly if I want to shave wet I'll use a blade. The only downside is that you really can't do fine shaping, like trim the edge of a sideburn, with the circular blades. There's no pop-up trimmer.<br /><br />Of course, there's a separate trimmer head, which does a decent, but not great, job on beard edges, back of the neck, etc., and it comes with an adjustable guide that allows you to make stubble if you prefer. A dedicated trimmer--or even the pop-up trimmer on my other razor does a cleaner job. The third head, a foil head for body shaving, is something I don't use, but I tried it out and not surprisingly it works best if you've already trimmed the long hairs, which you could do with the beard trimmer, and then use the body shaver for maintenance. You could use the face shaver on your body the same way, although it might be a little slower.<br /><br />Someone who will use all three functions will find this less expensive than buying three devices, and it's well-priced if you like the SensoTouch floating head design and don't mind having only the two heads. But if you mostly need a face shaver and want rotary baldes, you can get a low-end three-head Norelco that works about as well, and has a pop-up trimmer, for less than half the price.<br /><br />One other issue: it comes without any protective cover for the rotating blades, or carry case, so you'll have to improvise if you want to travel with it.

I much prefer a shaver with three rotary heads since the three heads will make the shaving process quicker as it covers more skin surface. Although I could hear the two rotary heads shaving the surface of my face, I found that I had to constantly go over spots as the shave was not as close as I prefer. Shaving with the two rotary heads takes longer than shaving with a razor with three rotary heads, an important factor when I am trying to get to work on time.<br /><br />Norelco also offers a styler attachment, with five length settings to provide maximum choice for facial hair. Additionally, the bodygroom attachment trims and shaves body hair. The bodygroom attachment is designed with rounded combs and tips to prevent skin irritation and seems to do the job well. The razor also is safe to use in the shower, and the battery is rated to last 40 minutes between charges.<br /><br />Bottom line, I like the Norelco Click & Style Shave Toolkit. I like the flexibility of the three interchangeable attachments and the fact that the razor can be used in the shower. I have had very good luck with Norelco razors over the years, and I suspect this one will provide the same quality. The one negative for me is the fact that the shaver attachment only has two rotary heads. I prefer a razor with three rotary heads to save time and provide a closer shave.

It just plain breaks quickly making it a rather useless product. -------- I have been using Norelco electric shavers after my father introduced me to them decades ago. At that time there weren't even cordless razors available. The rotary design is superior in all regards to all foil razors. The reason is that the foil design capture hairs as effectively. I was given a Braun top of the line foil razor several years ago, and it was OK, but I would take out my cheap old corded (very old) Norelco to finish the job at times because it would repeatedly pass over areas of my face without removing the hair. So, I have stuck with Norelco brand, but I have been having a problem with all their products of late. Trimmers, razors and even a novel hair cutting tool they sell for cutting your own hair (does a quite acceptable job) have all had battery problems within weeks of purchase. The batteries on all of them are horrible. On the first week of use, they are fine, and then decline rapidly. This shaver now sounds anemic after several weeks use even when it has been charged for hours and cleaned. And these will not operate off of a plug. It will only charge the battery. If it could run off of an outlet, I would just leave it plugged in, but it won't. It doesn't run out of power during a shave, it just deteriorates quickly to the point where the blades are barely spinning. Still shaves OK, but much more slowly. My other Norelco products have died altogether after about a year and became anemic within a month of purchase. One holds a charge for a minute before it beeps loudly and shuts off. Another won't charge at all after about six months of use. I want to replace the batteries, but they cost so much it doesn't seem worth it, especially if they are of the same quality as the originals.. So, overall, these are great razors, but I have had this battery problem so often with them, I cannot recommend them without a warning about the battery life. The Braun I had doesn't shave that great, but the battery is strong and willing after several years. I use it frequently for trimming but I still don't shave with it. This works well on the face and body, so if the battery was better, I would classify it a five star product.

While the resulting shave was not blade shave close, it was still a very close shave with hardly any missed whiskers and very few scratchy, stubbly spots.   379. The Philips Norelco YS524/41 Click & Style Shave Toolkit is a decent electric razor and groomer. It comes with three separate attachments, an electric face razor, a beard trimmer, and a body shaver. All three attach easily by snapping on and can similar detach easily by pulling off. All pieces are easy to clean: just run under hot water and use the provided brush as necessary to get all the excess hair out. The base handle piece is a bit big and bulky but is comfortable to hold. While the battery life is quoted as 40 minutes, I actually found it to be probably about twice that, and it seemed to die without warning. My impressions of the three attachments are as follows:<br /><br />The razor is a typical &#34;safe&#34; razor style in which you should theoretically not be able to cut yourself by shaving (however, I actually drew blood yesterday while using it). It contours to your face as you move it around your cheek and jawline. While it generally works well, it has some drawbacks. I have found that I can never get a full clean shave with it and still have to keep my traditional hand razor to clean up remaining hairs that it misses or to hit my sideburns or the sides of my goatee. Since the razor is circular it has a difficult time hitting edges like that. Also, it is incredibly slow to use. I can shave much, much faster with a regular hand razor.<br /><br />The beard trimmer has an adjustable piece that attaches to the trimming unit so that you can adjust the closeness of the blades to your face. I've found it to be a bit frustrating to get it just right, as when I hold the razor upright (that is, with the handle pointing down) I can't seem to get much progress in trimming my facial hair; contrarily, I can hold it the other way with the handle pointing up and it will overtrim.<br /><br />The body shaver is frustrating, to say the least. It consists of a regular metal shaver/blades like the other two pieces, and also has a plastic attachment that serves as a &#34;comb&#34; while shaving. I have found the comb to be not much use, as not much comes off while using it, and unfortunately without it the blades pull a bit painfully. I find this attachment to be the least useful.<br /><br />All in all I would say that this grooming toolkit is decent, but would recommend something else if you can find one that is better reviewed.
  380. The standard against which a multiple use product like this is to be measured is NOT whether it is the best performing product at each task, but rather whether it performs well enough to replace two or more items in your bathroom or more importantly in your carry on luggage. As a habitually clean-shaven man, I might seem a poor choice to review such a product, but a fortuitously timed Great Recession has allowed me to grow a beard in order to fully test the device.<br /><br />BEARD STYLING HEAD: The beard styling trimmer is pretty basic, having no vacuum and only 5 length settings: 11/64, 9/64, 7/64, 5/64, and 3/64 inch. The length lock is mechanical and seems pretty steady; it never \\"slipped\\" on me. The beard styling comb is removable for contouring. Note: At the shortest length as well as with the comb removed, the blade is quite close to the skin, making it relatively easy to cut yourself.<br /><br />SHAVER HEAD: As a blade shaver whose weapon of choice is the [[ASIN:B003987CL0 Gillette Fusion Proglide Men's Power Razor]], I have always believed that electric razors are for men who don't really insist on a close shave (or less facetiously for men whose lifestyle requires shaving on-the-go). Nothing about the performance of this trimmer's shaver head has changed my mind, and for shaving the entire face it is clearly inferior to any of their more advanced triple headed shavers. However, in fairness, it was never really intended for this purpose. No man in his right mind would choose such a product unless he was planning to at least experiment with facial hair, and for the purpose of shaving (wet or dry) those parts of your face not covered by your beard or mustache, it is quite adequate, while for shaving your whole face, it gets the job done eventually.<br /><br />GROOMER HEAD: Chances are this is going to be the selling point. There are lots of beard trimmer/shavers out there, but Philips made its name in body grooming, and what you get here is the very same revolutionary; wet, dry, or in the shower; dual-sided trimming blades with shaver foil in the middle [[ASIN:B000MN63CO Philips Norelco Bodygroom Trimmer/Shaver Foil]] that was offered on their very first model. The Trimmer Combs have changed design only once and that was to make them bidirectional. Unlike their various model single use body groomers which come with three trimmer combs (Numbers 1, 2, 3), this model comes with only a single trimmer comb, the shortest one (Number 1); however, unless your body hair grooming style is Neat Wookie, this shouldn't be a problem. In any case you can use the longer combs from other current models, should you happen to own one, like for example the [[ASIN:B007VB50JC Philips Norelco BG2028 Bodygroom]], or Philips Norelco will no doubt sell them to you as replacement parts.<br /><br />Note: Unless you plan on regularly maintaining yourself in that condition, it is not advisable to shave yourself too closely between the waist and the knees. Two words -- \\"razor stubble\\" -- in close contact with your most tender areas should be explanation enough.<br /><br />Note: Another option for those looking for the closest possible grooming is the [[ASIN:B001VEK1GW Braun BodyCruzer Men's Body Groomer, Titanium]]. Though the trimmer head is inferior to any Philips Norelco Bodygroom IMHO, its ace in the hole is the attachment for a [[ASIN:B003EMXLIE Gillette Fusion Cartridge]]. You cannot get a closer body shave than that. You could also try the new [[ASIN:B00HF3XSRW Gillette Body Razor]], essentially a [[ASIN:B0001LQGFG Gillette Venus Divine Sensitive Women's Razor]] with a color change, for that closest possible body shave finish.<br /><br />A much bigger problem IMHO, which cost this product a star in my review, was their redesign of the handle so that it cannot fit into the Back Shave Attachment that comes with their [[ASIN:B007VB50LU Philips Norelco BG2038 Bodygroom Plus]]. Depending on the length and flexibility of your arms, the acreage and thickness of your backwoods, or the presence of a partner willing to help you clear the underbrush on a regular basis, this might not be an issue for you, in which case you can add that star back. However, if when you wear a mesh shirt, no one looking at your back can tell you are wearing a shirt, you should probably give this some thought.<br /><br />Note: Should you be attempting to share living quarters with a smaller massed, higher voiced person who complains about being cold all the time, this body groomer may offer a solution because I have noted that after removing my fur I feel noticeably cooler and can tolerate a higher thermostat setting. Should said always cold person be willing to assist you in regular shearings, the potential for peaceful compromise could be greatly increased.he acreage and thickness of your backwoods, or the presence of a partner willing to help you clear the underbrush on a regular basis, this might not be an issue for you, in which case you can add that star back.   381. I've been looking for some kind of \\"all-in-one\\" shaver for a while now to use mostly when traveling or on vacation - having to carry two or three separate shavers/trimmers is cumbersome. I also wanted to try out a 2-head version of Norelco's rotary heads because the 3-head versions I have owned always felt a bit clumsy to me.<br /><br />The Click & Style got pretty good reviews and was available at a decent price so I gave it a try. I would be inclined, however, to call this an \\"entry-level\\" product as the plastics and parts feel a little on the cheap side. Also, no stand or carry bag is included with this item. Plus, when you store this thing in a drawer or cabinet there are always bits of stubble left in the heads and attachments that invariably make a mess in the bottom of a drawer or travel bag after a few months.<br /><br />I've been using this shaver a couple of times a weeks for about a month now. Performance of the 2-head shave head was fairly good. I was, however, very surprised (and disappointed) that the heads don't pivot! This made the shaving experience much more difficult than necessary. I had to move the whole shaver about to follow the contours of my face, instead of the heads flexing to follow the curves. But after a few days I got used to the shaver and was able to get a pretty close shave in the end.<br /><br />Because I only shave about twice a week it's necessary for me to first \\"pre-shave\\" the longer stubble on my face with the bare trimmer attachment. (Otherwise, shaving with the rotary heads alone, it would take about 20 minutes to shave down the long stubble!) I have a goatee, so I trim around that during the \\"pre-shave\\". The trimmer blades on this unit are of a fairly coarse design intended for rapid cutting, but at the expense of precision. My dedicated beard trimmer (also a Norelco) has a trimmer attachment with very fine (close together) blades, that produces a much neater edge to my goatee than the Click & Style trimmer does.<br /><br />The motor on this shaver feels a little underpowered most of the time, like it's just strong enough to do the job, but it starts bogging down (and pulling hairs) as soon as the battery starts to run down a bit. Since this is more of an entry-level product it uses a NiMH battery instead of a more powerful lithium-ion battery. As long as the shaver is used (and charged) regularly this isn't much of a problem, but if you only use it monthly you may find the battery has worn down quite a lot as NiMH batteries self-discharge quite rapidly. Run time overall was satisfactory, as I was able to get about three full shaves on a charge.<br /><br />I used the body trimmer only a bit to trim some areas on my neck and back. I actually had my girlfriend do the back trimming as I couldn't see or reach back there. It did a satisfactory job the two times we used it.<br /><br />In conclusion, if you're in the market for a shaver, a beard trimmer, and a body trimmer, the Philips Norelco YS524/41 Click & Style Shave Toolkit is a pretty good value over purchasing three separate devices. But because it is more of an entry-level product it doesn't really EXCEL at any of these functions. It will be great for my purposes as a unit I will use when traveling, but for my day to day shaving I will continue to use my superior individual products.<br /><br />*** MARGINALLY RECOMMENDED - 3 STARS ***es, that produces a much neater edge to my goatee than the Click & Style trimmer does.<br /><br />The motor on this shaver feels a little underpowered most of the time, like it's just strong enough to do the job, but it starts bogging down (and pulling hairs) as soon as the battery starts to run down a bit.   455. ===Overview===<br /><br />I was hesitant to buy this product after reading several reviews talk about the unit being low-powered. Unfortunately, I decided to go ahead and try out the item anyways since it comes with a 45 day money-back guarantee (more on that later). It arrived today, and I let it charge for several hours prior to using it as per the instructions. The take away story is that I was really unimpressed, and I'll go ahead and review the various components of the device in detail below.<br /><br />===Beard Trimmer===<br /><br />What I wanted:<br /><br />This is my first shaver/body groomer but not my first beard trimmer. I personally like to keep a 5-o'clock shadow look so I tend to just use a cheap Remington trimmer without the comb. I was hoping that this Norelco would be a more sophisticated machine and give me a more even trim. I looked at the specs and noted that the shortest length cut was about 1mm, I would have preferred something a bit closer but it seemed like this was pretty universal so I just went with it. All I really wanted from Norelco here was less irritation and a more even trim.<br /><br />What I got:<br /><br />The trimmer worked fine, the comb was essentially useless since I wanted the closest stubble I could get to really have that 5-o'clock shadow look. It was less irritating to the skin than my 30 dollar Remington trimmer, but not really that much more even. Nothing more to really say here, I didn't get a chance to use this on body hair because the battery died (more on that later).<br /><br />===Shaver===<br /><br />What I wanted:<br /><br />When I want to shave I go ahead and use a safety razor with BlueBird blades, so I had absolutely no expectation for the Norelco to give me a closer shave than that. What I did want from the Norelco was a fast shave that would be passable in case I was in a hurry and needed to look professional.<br /><br />What I got:<br /><br />I don't know if this is because im not used to electric shavers, but this really took me a while. Like, it took long enough that I think I could have just done a single pass with my safety razor and probably have gotten a closer shave. I have some really stubborn spots down at my neck that even my razor can't easily get where the Norelco really struggled. Some hairs it completely missed, I had to keep going over the same area to finally get a full shave. Where it did shave it did an alright job, but not really a close shave as I could still see a faint shadow-beard.<br /><br />Ultimately, I felt like the shaver gave me a very mediocre shave without saving me that much time compared to my safety razor.<br /><br />===Body Groomer===<br /><br />What I wanted:<br /><br />I was most excited about this attachment, and this was ultimately the reason why I wanted to branch out from just my old Remington beard trimmer. The Remington did an alright job doubling as a body groomer, but I wanted something that gave me the flexibility to shave bare as well as just trim. Also, beard trimmers are a bit dangerous at times when it comes to body grooming, so I was interested in a safe body grooming solution. The addition of a comb on this attachment was great because I could still choose to trim or go bare and still get the safety benefits.<br /><br />What I got:<br /><br />First I tried trimming down my chest hair with the combed body groomer. While I likes the length it trimmed to (which was lucky because this comb doesn't have different length settings), I didn't like how hard it was to shave evenly. I had to go over the same area many times because the hairs just didn't catch on the comb.<br /><br />So then I decided to try shaving the hairs on my stomach without the comb. The Norelco did a pretty decent job here, and usually got shorter hairs in the first two passes. Longer hairs were more of a challenge as they would easily evade being cut. Overall though, I liked being able to get a decent shave on my stomach without irritation, which is otherwise prone to ingrown hairs when using a razor blade. Nevertheless, I had a hard time getting hairs around the navel, and before I got to try other areas the battery died on the unit. It seems like this attachment really drains the juice.<br /><br />===Battery===<br /><br />I was a bit disappointed in the battery. I tried using the razor to do a partial test trim of the beard, then a shave, then I tried to do body grooming during which the battery died. This unit wont last long enough to get all your grooming done + a shave is the basic gist of this. So guys, you'll need to think carefully about what exactly you want shaved each day and account for the fact you may need to recharge this device to get everything done.<br /><br />===Money Back Guarantee===<br /><br />Right now I'm planning on sending this back to Norelco for their money back guarantee since I can't exactly return it to Amazon in \\"new\\" condition. Unfortunately, I didn't realize that the returns process to Norelco is a bit complicated, and involves waiting 3 weeks before you can send it back, filling out returns paperwork (that you apparently need to call a phone number to have mailed to you), paying shipping on the returns, and waiting 6-8 weeks for your check. Big hassle, and a huge head-ache.<br /><br />I'm going to wait the three weeks, if this machine miraculously becomes better I will update my review. Otherwise, just assume I shipped it back. I'll probably still be waiting for my check.herwise prone to ingrown hairs when using a razor blade.
